  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3ec7b47d-43d1-4dd4-a25f-e75cd12178d5'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer2023032005192956047">Princess Mia is dreaming about the prom - and contending with a hotel workers' strike - in the fifth, supremely hilarious episode of Meg Cabot's Princess Diaries. This time, Mia's in the pink about the upcoming Albert Einstein H.S. prom, and she's crossing her fingers that Michael will ask her to go. (They're in love, so why wouldn't he ask her, right?) But during Seven Mi</span>
  <span id="freeText2023032005192956047" style="display:none">Princess Mia is dreaming about the prom - and contending with a hotel workers' strike - in the fifth, supremely hilarious episode of Meg Cabot's Princess Diaries. This time, Mia's in the pink about the upcoming Albert Einstein H.S. prom, and she's crossing her fingers that Michael will ask her to go. (They're in love, so why wouldn't he ask her, right?) But during Seven Minutes in Heaven at her b-day party, Mia learns that Michael is not the prom-going type. Good grief, what's a princess to do? <br /><br />To make matters worse, Grandmere has gotten a busboy fired due to a mishap with her pooch, Rommel, at a swanky restaurant, so when all of the city's busboys go on strike, it causes a chain of events that result in Grandmere crashing at Mia's mom's place, her pal Lilly Moscovitz picking up a picket sign, and the prom being brought to a screeching halt. <br /><br />Thankfully, staunch yet boy-wise Grandmere has a plan to change Michael's mind and put everything back on track, making Mia the happiest "prom princess" on this side of the Atlantic - and readers more starry-eyed than Molly Ringwald in her prettiest pink frock. <br /><br />Following up the brief Volume IV and a Half and introducing a new addition to Mia's family, this knee-slapping fifth volume makes the series glitter brighter than ever, placing yet another jewel in Cabot's crown.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2023032005192956047" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_2068672').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_2068672').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_2068672').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer14910759336911266028"><blockquote>
  <i>"<b>Instead of being wakened to the sound of birdsong, like princesses in books, I was wakened to the sound of Rommel shrieking as Fat Louie beat him senseless for getting into his bowl of Fancy Feast</b>."</i>
</blockquote><br/>Fun as always.The Princess Diaries always make me feel better so I'm usually reading them when I'm kind of sad or depressed.Like this whole week.Today was my first day of senior year of high school and it was awful.The new school principal changed most of my professors.She also made a new behavio</span>
  <span id="freeText14910759336911266028" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"<b>Instead of being wakened to the sound of birdsong, like princesses in books, I was wakened to the sound of Rommel shrieking as Fat Louie beat him senseless for getting into his bowl of Fancy Feast</b>."</i>
</blockquote><br>Fun as always.The Princess Diaries always make me feel better so I'm usually reading them when I'm kind of sad or depressed.Like this whole week.Today was my first day of senior year of high school and it was awful.The new school principal changed most of my professors.She also made a new behavior/dressing codex &amp; stuff like that.Ugh,can this week get any worse?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395106490ra/8947209.gif" width="330" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Thankfully,this book lightened my mood.However,both Mia and Lilly were a bit annoying sometimes so I'm giving this book 4 stars.Can't wait to read the next one.<br><br>Favourite quotes:<br><br>"I only invited Michael to both the dinner and the party.Everyone else,including Lilly, is just invited to the party. <b>Hello, how unromantic would that be, to have your birthday dinner with your mom, your stepdad, your real dad, your grandma,your bodyguard, your boyfriend and his sister</b>. At least I was able to narrow it down a little."<br><br>“I can command the Royal Genovian Air Force," Grandmère supposedly replied. "As well as the Royal Genovian Navy. <b>But the one thing in the world I have no control over, Helen, is your womb</b>. Now come along.”</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer807275862147773501"><b>3 stars</b><br/><br/>Mia's neurosis, while entertaining, is starting to rub me the wrong way (<a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Yeah I get this was written 15 years ago but still let's not poke fun at disabilities, k? <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>). Also, 5 books to get through one year in the story is a bit much. I'm glad the others coming up are a bit more spread out.<br/><br/>But honestly, when it comes down to it, the <s>real</s> reason I'm here for this is to read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23215471-royal-wedding?ac=1&from_search=true' rel='nofollow noopener'>Royal Wedding</a> =D</span>

Also, 5 books to get through one year in the story is a bit much. I'm glad the others coming up are a bit more spread out.<br /><br />But honestly, when it comes down to it, the <s>real</s> reason I'm here for this is to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23215471-royal-wedding?ac=1&amp;from_search=true" rel="nofollow noopener">Royal Wedding</a> =D</span>

<div id="review_1172670867" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1172670867" />
    <a title="Nasty Lady MJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4026143-nasty-lady-mj"><img alt="Nasty Lady MJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506395877p2/4026143.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1172670867?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nasty Lady MJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nasty Lady MJ" href="/user/show/4026143-nasty-lady-mj">Nasty Lady MJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1172670867" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16788404112277541205">To see full binge for books 4, 41/3, 4 1/2, and 5 click <a href='https://howdyyal.wordpress.com/2015/02/01/the-unofficial-princess-diaries-binge-read-where-mia-gets-a-tad-bit-ocd/' rel='nofollow noopener'>here.</a><br/><br/>What I Remembered:<br/><br/> Really hating Lilly in this installment and not really feeling Toris.<br/><br/>What I Got:<br/><br/>Really hating Lilly. Finding Toris a lot more tolerable and believable. And finding Mia almost as intolerable as Lilly in this installment.<br/><br/>In fact, if I wanted to, I could have a drinking game every time Lilly or Mia annoyed me. I get that they’re fourteen/fifteen year old girls, but both of them need a good swift kick in the pants to rea</span>
  <span id="freeText16788404112277541205" style="display:none">To see full binge for books 4, 41/3, 4 1/2, and 5 click <a href="https://howdyyal.wordpress.com/2015/02/01/the-unofficial-princess-diaries-binge-read-where-mia-gets-a-tad-bit-ocd/" rel="nofollow noopener">here.</a><br /><br />What I Remembered:<br /><br /> Really hating Lilly in this installment and not really feeling Toris.<br /><br />What I Got:<br /><br />Really hating Lilly. Finding Toris a lot more tolerable and believable. And finding Mia almost as intolerable as Lilly in this installment.<br /><br />In fact, if I wanted to, I could have a drinking game every time Lilly or Mia annoyed me. I get that they’re fourteen/fifteen year old girls, but both of them need a good swift kick in the pants to reality.<br /><br />To be fair though, I did enjoy Princess in Pink a lot more than I remembered.<br /><br />I had some nice things going for it.<br /><br />For one, it had an actual plot (unlike Princess in Waiting) and their was some slight character development in this book.<br /><br />I think the best thing about this one was Michael. Sometimes I really wonder how he tolerates Mia so much though, because her neurosis is full blown in this one.<br /><br />He really must be the master of zen.<br /><br />The supporting characters though really carried this novel, save for Grandmere. I think this is the point where she starts developing into almost a caricature of sorts. But you could argue that about all the characters to a certain degree. Especially Lilly and Mia.<br /><br />I keep complaining about them…I guess I should discuss them.<br /><br />Lilly is just a horrible person. It’s a conclusion I came to a long time ago with these books, though she does have an entertaining moment or two when she’s not stuffing her tongue down some random guy’s throat. In this book, we don’t see those entertaining quirks since she’s mostly sticking her throat down some guy’s throat.<br /><br />Add to it, that Mia is sort of slut slamming her friend at the end with this little gem:<br /><br /><blockquote>Tina just called. She is kvelling over getting to go to the prom. It is, she says, like a dream come true. I told her I couldn’t agree more. She asked me how I thought we’d come to be so lucky.<br /><br />I told her: Because we are both kind and pure of heart (237).</blockquote><br /><br />Look, I get Lilly was really stupid in this installment. But as her best friend Mia shouldn’t quasi dis her to Tina with that stupid pure of heart trash. Then again, this is the girl that obsesses about her virginity to the point where she calls it her precious gift.<br /><br />And plus, it’s just prom.<br /><br />I think this is me being no longer fifteen. Maybe I could’ve agreed with Mia back then-maybe not.<br /><br />Despite my grievances with two of the characters, I did find this installment to be a huge improvement over Princess in Waiting. It’s fun and light, and actually has a plot.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16788404112277541205" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1372315191" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1372315191" />
    <a title="Claire - The Coffeeholic Bookworm" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19367448-claire---the-coffeeholic-bookworm"><img alt="Claire - The Coffeeholic Bookworm" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527053972p2/19367448.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1372315191?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Claire - The Coffeeholic Bookworm" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Claire - The Coffeeholic Bookworm" href="/user/show/19367448-claire---the-coffeeholic-bookworm">Claire - The Coffeeholic Bookworm</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1372315191" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12483527927345224168">This time around, Princess Mia looks forward to having the best dance of her life. By going to the prom. With her boyfriend, Michael. But the big problem is: Michael doesn’t want anything to do with prom.<br/><br/>Then there’s Grandmere who fires a busboy after something happens to her pet pooch. A strike among busboys ensue and soon Grandmere finds herself lodging in with Mia’s mom under one roof. Sounds exciting, eh? Oh but there’s more! Wait till you hear Mia’s moms exciting baby news!<br/><br/>After a while, yo</span>
  <span id="freeText12483527927345224168" style="display:none">This time around, Princess Mia looks forward to having the best dance of her life. By going to the prom. With her boyfriend, Michael. But the big problem is: Michael doesn’t want anything to do with prom.<br /><br />Then there’s Grandmere who fires a busboy after something happens to her pet pooch. A strike among busboys ensue and soon Grandmere finds herself lodging in with Mia’s mom under one roof. Sounds exciting, eh? Oh but there’s more! Wait till you hear Mia’s moms exciting baby news!<br /><br />After a while, you’d think I’ll get tired of reading Princess Diaries. But no. As long as I have this series in my shelf, I intend to finish them. My own sons even commented about my passion for reading this series. They thought I’m already too old for fairytales. Ouch, that quite stings!<br /><br />But then, I realized, kids are being kids and they already have a lot of opinions when it comes to the books they read. As young as they are (my sons are 10 and 8, respectively), they already know which books make them happy and which ones would make them roll their eyes. In this case, when they see me gawking and controlling my laughter, they retort, “Mom’s being childish again,” and then they will tell me, “It’s okay Mom, if that makes you happy, go on…”<br /><br />So there, Princess Amelia Migonette Thermopolis Renaldo, aka Mia, makes me happy. I don’t care much anymore if she’s too smitten with her boyfriend or too absorbed in her royal duties. Others might say, she’s too good to be true. But that’s exactly what I want in a princess. Not perfect, not too aristocratic, not too shabby either. Mia and her cohorts make the Princess Diaries more exciting and exhilarating to read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12483527927345224168" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1196587313" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1196587313" />
    <a title="kari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2207055-kari"><img alt="kari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1262446392p2/2207055.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1196587313?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="kari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="kari" href="/user/show/2207055-kari">kari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2207055-kari?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2207055-kari?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1196587313" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18304558583103965488">I'm reading this series in preparation for the <i> Royal Wedding</i>, the first adult novel about Mia, which is coming soon. I didn't start this series as an adolescent so my take on it is different then teen readers, but I think Cabot does have the emotions and hopes and dreams just right, or as I remember them anyway. The Prom is a big deal when you are in high school. And Mia wants to go.<br/>Even though she sees that she's lucky and most of her life is, at least for a moment, going well, she is pining f</span>
  <span id="freeText18304558583103965488" style="display:none">I'm reading this series in preparation for the <i> Royal Wedding</i>, the first adult novel about Mia, which is coming soon. I didn't start this series as an adolescent so my take on it is different then teen readers, but I think Cabot does have the emotions and hopes and dreams just right, or as I remember them anyway. The Prom is a big deal when you are in high school. And Mia wants to go.<br />Even though she sees that she's lucky and most of her life is, at least for a moment, going well, she is pining for a chance to go to the Prom with her boyfriend. She says she has dreamed of it her whole life. And while this may seem silly, I think it also rings true.<br />Mia's grandmother, as usual, causes problems for her, unintentionally perhaps in this case, but still, the repercussions, while funny, also move the story along.<br />I do have some trouble wondering why Mia continues to be friends with Lilly, who has in general been a bad friend, but in this book, takes that to a whole new level. Didn't much care for how she behaved, but hopefully in future books, she will do better toward Mia. Or Mia finds a new a better friend. Your friend should never put you down or humiliate you.<br />Great, fun read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18304558583103965488" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3631145464003806227">Now I can see why they didn't make anymore movies from this series. Also helps that when Anne Hathaway played Mia she wasn't fucking whiny all the god damn time.<br/><br/>I have no idea how I even got through this book but I'm having a feeling that I will need a bottle of wine while I read every other book in this series. <br/><br/>I liked Mia in the first book but now she's just so annoying.   <span id="freeText3631145464003806227" style="display:none">Now I can see why they didn't make anymore movies from this series. Also helps that when Anne Hathaway played Mia she wasn't fucking whiny all the god damn time.<br /><br />I have no idea how I even got through this book but I'm having a feeling that I will need a bottle of wine while I read every other book in this series. <br /><br />I liked Mia in the first book but now she's just so annoying. So, Mia whines a lot about going to prom in <i>Princess in Pink</i> and I don't understand why! I only went to my senior prom and trust me it was boring af. I don't get the whole school dance thing because you only really have fun at the after parties. Meh, maybe it's just me? <br /><br />Besides Mia being annoying, her friends are annoying too. This whole book was annoying. I don't even know how many times I wanted to throw this book or I rolled my eyes. Even though I know there are more books in this series that I want to read just so I can say I read this entire series - I also really want this to be the last book. Please pray for me.<br /><br /></span>

Because I know now what it is like to see all of your hopes and dreams crushed beneath the soulless heel of despair." Mia. Oh my god. It's prom. You are a freshman. How are they still friends?????????????<br /><br />Also, Mia, please re-read Jane Eyre. </span>

<div id="review_1625029580" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1625029580" />
    <a title="Sara Saif" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33555642-sara-saif"><img alt="Sara Saif" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567114974p2/33555642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1625029580?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara Saif" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara Saif" href="/user/show/33555642-sara-saif">Sara Saif</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33555642-sara-saif?shelf=its-a-tie">its-a-tie</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1625029580" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13401032433393075151"><p>So this one was all about Mia’s heartfelt desire to go to prom with Michael which, in her opinion, would bring her one step closer to achieving self-actualization. (*insert scoffing sound*) Every book in a series has its protagonist facing great adversities. The enemy gets bigger and badder with each installment. In the Princess Diaries series, however, the “difficulties” Mia faces are:</p><p><br/>1-Who is going to take me to the Cultural Diversity Dance?<br/>2-Ditto Nondenominational Winter Dance.<br/>3-Will I ever </p></span>
  <span id="freeText13401032433393075151" style="display:none"><p>So this one was all about Mia’s heartfelt desire to go to prom with Michael which, in her opinion, would bring her one step closer to achieving self-actualization. (*insert scoffing sound*) Every book in a series has its protagonist facing great adversities. The enemy gets bigger and badder with each installment. In the Princess Diaries series, however, the “difficulties” Mia faces are:</p><p><br>1-Who is going to take me to the Cultural Diversity Dance?<br>2-Ditto Nondenominational Winter Dance.<br>3-Will I ever get a boyfriend?<br>4-Will I be able to have my first date with Michael?<br>And now Ladies and Gentleman, this:<br>5-WILL MICHAEL ASK ME TO GO TO PROM WITH HIM? WELL? WILL HE? WILL HE?<br>LOL. This stuff is so dumb, I love it.<br></p><p>All it took was the mere mentioning of prom by Shameeka, Mia’s friend, and that did it. Boy did she make use of EVERY WAKING MOMENT to obsess over it! She had this really really REALLY satisfying (for me) conversation with Lily about it in which Lily said everything I wanted to hear. She told Mia that her vegetarian diet was messing with her brain and she was going nuts and when Mia ranted about her life’s problems Lily said LIKE A BOSS,” You forgot to complain about your grandmother.”</p><br><br>I think at this point it is totally useless to repeat what I have already said about a thousand times already. I remember saying that I would “patiently” wait for Mia’s character growth. Scratch that. Scratch it real hard. Scratch it over and over again. All my patience has been flushed down the drain. I am past the point where I would actually care what she thinks or what she does. I have been pushed past my limits for her idiocy so many times that I have become immune to it. Like I said, the dumber it gets the more determined I become to finish this series.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462116624ra/18955885.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><p>The whole Boris/Lily thing was actually interesting. Lily was such a jerk-ass in this one. Mia’s writing got no further than the school menu, Rocky Thermopolis-Gianini was born, Tina and Boris got together and of course, Mia got to go to prom. The pattern of these books has become quite clear now. Obviously the writer knew she was going to write a lot of books so she made sure that as little as possible happens in each one. Aside from people getting together or people breaking up, what essentially happens is that Mia finds a new thing in each book to whine about, she <i>whines</i> about it while disregarding every good thing that has happened to her then she gets what she wants in the end. Rinse repeat.</p><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462116624ra/18955886.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440562522ra/15993096.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><p>Despite hating Mia’s guts, I kept reading and that is why it gets 3 stars. Now if you’ll excuse me, I have to go read the next book.</p><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="13401032433393075151" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_66165113" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/66165113" />
    <a title="Audrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2588512-audrey"><img alt="Audrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605974533p2/2588512.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/66165113?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Audrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Audrey" href="/user/show/2588512-audrey">Audrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2588512-audrey?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2588512-audrey?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2588512-audrey?shelf=real-life">real-life</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2588512-audrey?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer66165113&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer66165113" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9424348283661063337">Mia really, really, really, REALLY wants to go to prom with Michael. But Michael thinks prom is beyond idiotic. So she's upset. Essentially, this book is about Mia wanting to go to prom with Michael, and Lilly cheating on her boyfriend initially with a busboy that Grandmere got fired, creating a city-wide strike, and eventually breaking up with Boris, who ends up dumping a globe on his head to try to get her back, but then he ends up with Tina, so that's okay. But Lilly gets really mad, which is</span>
  <span id="freeText9424348283661063337" style="display:none">Mia really, really, really, REALLY wants to go to prom with Michael. But Michael thinks prom is beyond idiotic. So she's upset. Essentially, this book is about Mia wanting to go to prom with Michael, and Lilly cheating on her boyfriend initially with a busboy that Grandmere got fired, creating a city-wide strike, and eventually breaking up with Boris, who ends up dumping a globe on his head to try to get her back, but then he ends up with Tina, so that's okay. But Lilly gets really mad, which is kinda funny. I think that Lilly needs to realize that the world doesn't revolve around her. I mean, she just takes everything for granted. Like her friendship with Mia, I mean, seriously? Mia does everything that Lilly wants her to do. It's kinda annoying. Now, I'm not saying that the rest of us don't do that sometimes but still. So, Lilly has a new boyfriend. And since she created the strike, the prom is cancelled, making everyone even more upset. But then Grandmere pulls through and Mia is able to book Skinner Box, Michael's band, to play at the prom, so they get a gig and Mia gets to go to prom, even if she doesn't get to dance with Michael because he's playing, which I think is really stupid, and why would she even bother to go to prom? Like honestly, if you can't even dance with your boyfriend, then why bother??? Oh, and also in the middle of prom her mom has a baby, so then Mia has a little baby brother named Rocky, which is just adorable. And she essentially wants to raise him to be Michael, except prom loving. </span>

<div id="review_1436357001" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1436357001" />
    <a title="Sheida" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2313734-sheida"><img alt="Sheida" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310219911p2/2313734.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1436357001?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sheida" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sheida" href="/user/show/2313734-sheida">Sheida</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1436357001" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17325172233822397475">Next to Harry Potter, Princess Mia Thermopolis was probably the most formative literary character of my childhood. I remember being 13 and relating to every single word that was written in these books and feeling as though they were /my/ diaries and not Mia's. However, not surprisingly, reading them at 25 does not have quite the same impact. I no longer relate to Mia's self-centered obsessions about prom and I certainly no longer find Boris' manipulative self-destructive declaration of love even</span>
  <span id="freeText17325172233822397475" style="display:none">Next to Harry Potter, Princess Mia Thermopolis was probably the most formative literary character of my childhood. I remember being 13 and relating to every single word that was written in these books and feeling as though they were /my/ diaries and not Mia's. However, not surprisingly, reading them at 25 does not have quite the same impact. I no longer relate to Mia's self-centered obsessions about prom and I certainly no longer find Boris' manipulative self-destructive declaration of love even remotely romantic, but I do somewhat remember what it felt like to be 15 and oh so dramatic about /everything/. While the 10 year age difference between Mia and I does make me shake my head at quite a lot of the notions in the book, it doesn't make me dislike it. I view it as a window into the mind of the pretty oblivious and ignorant 15 year old that I used to be and it makes me all the more excited to continue with my re-read and to be reminded of how Mia grows up. Overall, if it wasn't for the sake of nostalgia, I would give this 3 stars but ... I just can't bring myself to do that tbh. <br /><br />EDIT: However, these covers are UGLY AS HECK, I'm glad my books have the old cartoon drawing of Mia and Fat Louie on the cover. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17325172233822397475" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1384751632" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1384751632" />
    <a title="Mehsi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6720768-mehsi"><img alt="Mehsi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588684075p2/6720768.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1384751632?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mehsi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mehsi" href="/user/show/6720768-mehsi">Mehsi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781447287766" href="/book/show/25801375-prom-princess">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6720768-mehsi?shelf=cover-love">cover-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6720768-mehsi?shelf=for-girls-one-shelf">for-girls-one-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6720768-mehsi?shelf=warning-english-books">warning-english-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6720768-mehsi?shelf=away-laughing-on-a-fast-camel">away-laughing-on-a-fast-camel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6720768-mehsi?shelf=4-twinkling-stars">4-twinkling-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1384751632" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13886964309609024594">After a disastrous 4th book, I was really worried about this series. Worried that it would just turn out to be all like this. And I didn't want that, so I went into this book with worry and I was looking at with different eyes. <br/><br/>Thankfully the book turned out to be great, a lot of fun and Mia was mostly doable in this one. Still a bit weird, still a bit strange, still a bit annoying, but I saw another girl as well. She is really growing up, she starting to see more of the world, starting to tell </span>
  <span id="freeText13886964309609024594" style="display:none">After a disastrous 4th book, I was really worried about this series. Worried that it would just turn out to be all like this. And I didn't want that, so I went into this book with worry and I was looking at with different eyes. <br /><br />Thankfully the book turned out to be great, a lot of fun and Mia was mostly doable in this one. Still a bit weird, still a bit strange, still a bit annoying, but I saw another girl as well. She is really growing up, she starting to see more of the world, starting to tell her opinion more clearly.<br />But, something that was a bit annoying was the prom stuff. On the one hand it was cute, but on the other hand, was it really necessary to have it going on and on for like 200+ pages? Can't she just have told him quicker, couldn't she have done something else? <br /><br />Her relationship with Michael is really cute and I love them together. I am also happy that the book doesn't shy away from talking about bases, and about Mia's questions about second bases and such. However, at times, especially with how Mia acts (not always like a 15 year old), it felt also weird. At times Mia felt like she was more like 12/13, while Michael stayed the same age for me, so yeah. Awkward. <br />But still, I feel that these 2 will be together for a long long time to come, they are truly a great match, and I hope that Meg Cabot won't shy away from further topics, as I feel that it is what makes this series so great. That she dares to talk about stuff like this, and it also makes Mia seem more realistic. After all what girl of her age doesn't think about stuff like that. <br /><br />Michael, while I did like him in the previous books, I didn't always like him in this. That he didn't have a clue what Mia would like, that he was so stand-offish about prom and didn't get that he hurt Mia in the process. That he wouldn't even let his prejudices go away for her, for the girl he apparently loves. <br />But he was also sweet, and I loved him at the end and what he did there. Not everyone dares to speak up like that, so I applaud him for doing that. <br /><br />We also have 3 special events happening in this book. Mia's birthday (and the disaster that that was), the birth of Mia's sibling, and the prom. I won't say if it is a brother or sister, you will just have to read the book to find out, but I was delighted with the name they picked.<br /><br />Grandmere, still one of the characters I truly hate the most. At times she has some sweet moments, but mostly she is just so annoying and apparently thinks she is above everyone and everything and I hate that kind of attitude. She should see that she is only hurting people, that she is only being a bitch.<br /><br />The last thing that I want to address in my review is Lily. I always didn't particularly like Lily. I don't mind strong-willed, strong-minded characters, but Lily? Lily is just a bitch. Lily is just annoying. And what she did in this book? I am not one to call someone a slut immediately, but sorry, with what she did in this book? For once I will let my resolution go. What a slut. What a bitch move to do. Seriously, what the hell is wrong with you. And then that ending part? Convenient amnesia is what I would call it. This is not how relationships work, this is not what you do. But then again, it is not the first time that Lily can't see more than 2 centimetres in front of her, and if something makes her look bad (even if it is the truth) she will just ignore it or make up something totally different. This behaviour is disgusting. I hope that Lily will soon grow up out of this horrendous behaviour. I truly can't see how she and Mia are friends. Often she chews out Mia, instead of helping she says harsh and mean things, and while I am guessing that Lily will always be Mia's friend, I hope that Mia will go to Tina or Shameeka more in the future, and that she will just let Lily alone.<br /><br />All in all though, this was a good part in the series, and I am delighted it wasn't as bad as I thought it would be! :D<br /><br />I can't wait until January when book 6 and 7 come out (no clue why all of the sudden there is like 4 months between the books (this one, the 4th book, the 2nd and 3rd, and the first one all came out from July to August, and now we have to wait so long?)). <br /><br />Review first posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://twirlingbookprincess.com/">http://twirlingbookprincess.com/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13886964309609024594" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_369999159" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/369999159" />
    <a title="Tricia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7420220-tricia"><img alt="Tricia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443717541p2/7420220.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/369999159?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tricia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tricia" href="/user/show/7420220-tricia">Tricia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">whiny teenage girls</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7420220-tricia?shelf=facepalm">facepalm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7420220-tricia?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7420220-tricia?shelf=never-again">never-again</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer369999159" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11503863304608937732">Whine whine whine whine whine. Bella out of <i>Twilight</i> is a better narrator than Mia. Still, we can draw some similarities, can't we? Both stories start out with precarious yet vaguely original ideas (high school princess/vampire boyfriend) and both get sidetracked with unrelated, self-absorbed rants that completely murder any potential plot or action (why won't he take me to prom/why won't he make me a vampire). You get the gist of it. I didn't have much of a problem with either series until they</span>
  <span id="freeText11503863304608937732" style="display:none">Whine whine whine whine whine. Bella out of <i>Twilight</i> is a better narrator than Mia. Still, we can draw some similarities, can't we? Both stories start out with precarious yet vaguely original ideas (high school princess/vampire boyfriend) and both get sidetracked with unrelated, self-absorbed rants that completely murder any potential plot or action (why won't he take me to prom/why won't he make me a vampire). You get the gist of it. I didn't have much of a problem with either series until they started taking that route.<br /><br />More than anything, Mia is just shallow and horrible. Worse than Bella. You heard me. WORSE THAN BELLA. I mean, <i>some</i> bratty protagonists at least know to stop before they cross the hypocrisy border. But no. For five books now, Mia's been complaining about how she's such a freak, but continues to scorn others and write them off as... you guessed it: freaks. And we're supposed to like her <i>why?</i><br /><br />What got to me the most was this little fear she had halfway through the "story" about whether or not she might have Aspergers syndrome. Now I'm sure it must be pretty life-changing if you were to realise that in your teens. But to me, this was just another thing she could complain about, another thing she could claim makes her unfairly different to everyone else. How is that a good message to send out? I know many people with Aspergers and they're all lovely - and in my view, just like ordinary people. I seemed to read this as "OMG! I might have this syndrome thingy, I'm such a freak!" and I just thought, no. That is not how you talk about Aspergers syndrome. Come back when you've written a remotely sensitive or politically correct novel. And, you know, having a likeable heroine might help too.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11503863304608937732" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13027357376300217327">Okay, now Mia is totally getting on my nerves. Why isn’t she growing up a little? I never realised teens complained so much about EVERYTHING! She basically thinks every single issue that comes up and that doesn’t go along her way is ruining her life.   <span id="freeText13027357376300217327" style="display:none">Okay, now Mia is totally getting on my nerves. Why isn’t she growing up a little? I never realised teens complained so much about EVERYTHING! She basically thinks every single issue that comes up and that doesn’t go along her way is ruining her life. It’s time to get some perspective, Mia. <br /><br />It really peeved me to see how obsessed she was with the prom. I mean, the word “prom” is mentioned a whopping 287 times in the book! And it wasn’t even HER senior prom! It was Michael’s. And he was least interested in it. Truly, this book is the first one in the series that took me so long to finish. I just didn’t care for Mia’s obsession with Michael’s senior prom and the recurring issue of Lilly protesting for Jangbu Pinasa getting fired because of something Mia’s grandmother did in a restaurant during Mia’s birthday dinner. Moreover, Lilly breaking up with Boris in such an insensitive manner just drove me up the wall. I’m disappointed and seriously contemplating moving on to the next book. Please, Mia. Please just grow up now. <br /><br />Also, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Tina and Boris do seem cute together <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. But,as always, Michael is the light at the end of the tunnel and currently my only hope going further into the series.<br /></span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_51530580'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/51530580-malice"><img alt="Malice" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1597242210l/51530580._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xszq9RoxY4vCGTeucRRgtwr/ma7At0zKW6Uju+Q+jmq6e8UjOKISCl+0pb4rVQWiJJNJ+euDOu6ucIP3wH/uYg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('R4PqETamINfRrxXGTvd7eMQC+0D7w9+eCZn32BUllPw7NMXHFDVRVkwCh9YUth5t6m4rF9D3qbr8TFeUMWT09A==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10314091304573412237">Librarian note: AKA <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/167932.Jenny_Carroll' title='Jenny Carroll' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jenny Carroll</a> (1-800-Where-R-You series), AKA <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/71187.Patricia_Cabot' title='Patricia Cabot' rel='nofollow noopener'>Patricia Cabot</a> (historical romance novels).<br/><br/>Meg Cabot was born on February 1, 1967, during the Chinese astrological year of the Fire Horse, a notoriously unlucky sign. Fortunately she grew up in Bloomington, Indiana, where few people were aware of the stigma of being a fire horse -- at least until Meg became a teenager, when she flun</span>
  <span id="freeText10314091304573412237" style="display:none">Librarian note: AKA <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/167932.Jenny_Carroll" title="Jenny Carroll" rel="nofollow noopener">Jenny Carroll</a> (1-800-Where-R-You series), AKA <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/71187.Patricia_Cabot" title="Patricia Cabot" rel="nofollow noopener">Patricia Cabot</a> (historical romance novels).<br /><br />Meg Cabot was born on February 1, 1967, during the Chinese astrological year of the Fire Horse, a notoriously unlucky sign. Fortunately she grew up in Bloomington, Indiana, where few people were aware of the stigma of being a fire horse -- at least until Meg became a teenager, when she flunked freshman Algebra twice, then decided to cut her own bangs. After six years as an undergrad at Indiana University, Meg moved to New York City (in the middle of a sanitation worker strike) to pursue a career as an illustrator, at which she failed miserably, forcing her to turn to her favorite hobby--writing novels--for emotional succor. She worked various jobs to pay the rent, including a decade-long stint as the assistant manager of a 700 bed freshmen dormitory at NYU, a position she still occasionally misses. <br /><br />She is now the author of nearly fifty books for both adults and teens, selling fifteen million copies worldwide, many of which have been #1 New York Times bestsellers, most notably The Princess Diaries series, which is currently being published in over 38 countries, and was made into two hit movies by Disney. In addition, Meg wrote the Mediator and 1-800-Where-R-You? series (on which the television series, Missing, was based), two All-American Girl books, Teen Idol, Avalon High, How to Be Popular, Pants on Fire, Jinx, a series of novels written entirely in email format (Boy Next Door, Boy Meets Girl, and Every Boy's Got One), a mystery series (Size 12 Is Not Fat/ Size 14 Is Not Fat Either/Big Boned), and a chick-lit series called Queen of Babble. <br /><br />Meg is now writing a new children's series called Allie Finkle's Rules for Girls. Her new paranormal series, Abandon, debuts in Summer of 2011. <br /><br />Meg currently divides her time between Key West, Indiana, and New York City with a primary cat (one-eyed Henrietta), various back-up cats, and her husband, who doesn't know he married a fire horse. Please don't tell him. <br /><br /><br /><b>Series:</b><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/45023-airhead" rel="nofollow noopener">Airhead</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/43768-the-princess-diaries" rel="nofollow noopener">The Princess Diaries</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/41667-mediator" rel="nofollow noopener">Mediator</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10314091304573412237" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
